{
  "content": "# Kubernetes APF QueueSet: Algorithmic Deep-Dive\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nThe QueueSet subsystem implements **Fair Queuing for Server Requests (FQSR)**, a specialized fair-queuing algorithm that multiplexes concurrent API server requests across priority levels. It provides weighted fairness guarantees through virtual time scheduling, shuffle-sharded queue assignment, and adaptive dispatch based on estimated work (seat-seconds). This document traces the end-to-end control flow, dissects the fairness algorithm, and discusses operational tradeoffs.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n### 1.1 Purpose\n\nThe QueueSet is the **execution scheduling engine** of API Priority and Fairness (APF). It sits between the APF filter (which classifies requests) and the main request handler (which executes them). Its role:\n\n- **Admission control**: Reject or queue requests when concurrency limits are exceeded\n- **Fair dispatch**: Select which queued request executes next, ensuring:\n  - Proportional fairness among flows (via virtual time)\n  - Starvation prevention (via round-robin queue selection)\n  - Work-aware scheduling (via seat-seconds, not just request count)\n- **Concurrency accounting**: Track occupied \"seats\" (a logical concurrency unit) across phases of request execution\n\n### 1.2 Boundaries\n\n**Upstream dependencies:**\n- **APF Controller** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_controller.go`): Provides `QueuingConfig` (desired number of queues, queue length limit, hand size for shuffle sharding) and `DispatchingConfig` (concurrency limit)\n- **Request classifiers**: Extract flow distinguisher and match requests to priority levels\n- **Work estimators** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/request/width.go`): Estimate request width (initial seats, final seats, additional latency) based on request type and payload size\n\n**Downstream dependencies:**\n- **HTTP handler**: Calls `StartRequest()`, then `req.Finish()` when done\n- **Metrics subsystem** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/metrics/`): Observes request counts, seat occupancy, dispatch latencies, rejections\n- **Event clock** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/eventclock/`): Provides virtual time ticking and delayed event scheduling\n\n### 1.3 Key Data Dependencies\n\n- **WorkEstimate**: Carries `InitialSeats` (concurrency during main phase), `FinalSeats` (reserved after execution), and `AdditionalLatency` (padding duration)\n- **SeatSeconds**: Fixed-point representation of work = seats \u00d7 duration, with 1e8 internal scale factor\n- **QueuingConfig**: Encodes desired number of queues (0 = bypass queueing, negative = exempt), queue length limit, shuffle-sharding hand size\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### 2.1 Core Types\n\n#### `queueSet` (queueset.go:85\u2013167)\nThe main orchestrator. Fields include:\n- **`queues []*queue`**: Array of FIFO queues, allocated per shuffle-sharded flow\n- **`currentR fqrequest.SeatSeconds`**: Global virtual time progress meter (R from fair queuing)\n- **`lock sync.Mutex`**: Protects all mutable state\n- **`totSeatsInUse`, `totSeatsWaiting`**: Aggregate seat occupancy\n- **`totRequestsWaiting`, `totRequestsExecuting`**: Request counts for metrics\n- **`dCfg fq.DispatchingConfig`**: Concurrency limits and seat accounting denominators\n- **`promiseFactory`**: Creates decision promises (deferred-write channels for async dispatch decisions)\n\n**Responsibilities:**\n- Initial request ingress and rejection (via `StartRequest()`)\n- Virtual time progression and epoch management\n- Dispatch loop orchestration\n- Request completion tracking and seat release\n\n#### `queue` (types.go:93\u2013110)\nPer-flow-distinguisher queue. Fields:\n- **`requestsWaiting fifo`**: Ordered list of queued requests\n- **`requestsExecuting sets.Set[*request]`**: Executing requests from this queue (for seat tracking)\n- **`nextDispatchR fqrequest.SeatSeconds`**: Virtual finish time of next dispatch from this queue\n- **`seatsInUse int`**: Occupied seats in this queue\n\n**Responsibilities:**\n- FIFO ordering of requests awaiting dispatch\n- Virtual time tracking per queue (anti-windup mechanism)\n\n#### `request` (types.go:33\u201383)\nRequest wrapper with scheduling metadata. Fields:\n- **`decision promise.WriteOnce`**: Deferred decision (execute/cancel)\n- **`arrivalTime`, `startTime`**: Real timestamps for latency metrics\n- **`arrivalR fqrequest.SeatSeconds`**: Virtual time at arrival\n- **`workEstimate completedWorkEstimate`**: Computed total work (initial + final)\n\n**Responsibilities:**\n- Carries request context and work estimate\n- Defers dispatch decision via promise pattern (allows async decision-setting under lock, decision-reading without lock)\n\n#### `requestFIFO` (fifo_list.go:71\u2013156)\nLinked-list FIFO with aggregate statistics. Methods:\n- **`Enqueue(req)`**: Returns `removeFromFIFOFunc` for O(1) removal\n- **`QueueSum()`**: Returns aggregated `InitialSeatsSum`, `MaxSeatsSum`, `TotalWorkSum`\n- **`Walk(func)`**: Iterates without copying (permits removal during iteration)\n\n**Responsibilities:**\n- O(1) enqueue/dequeue/remove operations\n- Maintains running sums of seated widths for shuffle-sharding decisions\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Control Flow\n\n### 3.1 Request Arrival: `StartRequest()` (queueset.go:308\u2013356)\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500 StartRequest(ctx, workEstimate, hashValue, ...)\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500 Step 0: Check if queueing is bypassed\n\u2502  \u2502  (DesiredNumQueues < 1 \u2192 concurrency-only mode)\n\u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u251c\u2500 If queues disabled:\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2514\u2500 Call canAccommodateSeatsLocked(workEstimate.MaxSeats)\n\u2502  \u2502     \u251c\u2500 If yes: dispatchSansQueueLocked() \u2192 return request (immediate exec)\n\u2502  \u2502     \u2514\u2500 If no: increment totRequestsRejected, return (nil, isIdleLocked)\n\u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2514\u2500 If queues enabled: proceed to Step 1\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500 Step 1: Shuffle-shard and enqueue\n\u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u251c\u2500 shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked()\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502  \u251c\u2500 Call shuffleShardLocked(hashValue)\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502  \u2502  Uses dealer.DealIntoHand(hashValue) to get candidate queues\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502  \u2502  Selects queue with minimum TotalWorkSum (load-balanced assignment)\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502  \u2514\u2500 Return queue index\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502  \u251c\u2500 Create request object with:\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502  \u251c\u2500 arrivalTime \u2190 clock.Now()\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502  \u251c\u2500 arrivalR \u2190 currentR (current virtual time)\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502  \u251c\u2500 decision \u2190 promiseFactory(nil) [decision not yet set]\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502  \u2514\u2500 workEstimate \u2190 completeWorkEstimate(workEstimate)\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502  \u251c\u2500 Call rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked(request)\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502  \u251c\u2500 If totSeatsInUse >= concurrencyLimit AND queueLength >= queueLengthLimit:\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502  \u2502  \u2514\u2500 REJECT (return false)\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502  \u2514\u2500 Else: enqueueToBoundLocked(request)\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502     \u251c\u2500 If queue empty: queue.nextDispatchR \u2190 currentR (initialize virtual start)\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502     \u251c\u2500 queue.requestsWaiting.Enqueue(request)\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502     \u251c\u2500 totRequestsWaiting++, totSeatsWaiting += request.MaxSeats()\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502     \u2514\u2500 Metrics: AddRequestsInQueues, AddSeatsInQueues\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2514\u2500 If rejected: return nil\n\u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2514\u2500 If enqueued: proceed to Step 2\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500 Step 2: Immediate dispatch as much as possible\n\u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2514\u2500 dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()\n\u2502     \u2502  While totRequestsWaiting > 0 AND totSeatsInUse < concurrencyLimit:\n\u2502     \u2502    \u2514\u2500 dispatchLocked() (see Section 3.2)\n\u2502     \u2502\n\u2502     \u2514\u2500 Executes requests from queues until concurrency limit or no queued requests\n\u2502\n\u2514\u2500 Return (request, false)\n   \u2502  If request is nil: caller should reject\n   \u2502  If request is non-nil: caller must call request.Finish() when done\n```\n\n### 3.2 Dispatch: `dispatchLocked()` and Fair Queue Selection (queueset.go:695\u2013743)\n\nFair Queuing uses **virtual time** to achieve fairness. Key insight: dispatch the request whose virtual *finish time* is earliest, ensuring proportional service allocation.\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500 dispatchLocked()\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500 findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked()\n\u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u251c\u2500 Iterate round-robin through queues\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2514\u2500 For each queue with waiting requests:\n\u2502  \u2502     \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502     \u251c\u2500 Peek oldest request\n\u2502  \u2502     \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502     \u251c\u2500 Compute currentVirtualFinish:\n\u2502  \u2502     \u2502  \u2502  = queue.nextDispatchR + oldestRequest.totalWork()\n\u2502  \u2502     \u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502     \u2502  \u2502  Where totalWork = InitialSeats\u00d7EstimatedServiceDuration\n\u2502  \u2502     \u2502  \u2502                     + FinalSeats\u00d7AdditionalLatency\n\u2502  \u2502     \u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502     \u2502  \u2514\u2500 If currentVirtualFinish < minVirtualFinish:\n\u2502  \u2502     \u2502     \u2514\u2500 Record this queue as best candidate\n\u2502  \u2502     \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502     \u2514\u2500 Also track virtual dispatch start (nextDispatchR - estimatedWorkInProgress)\n\u2502  \u2502        for metrics\n\u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u251c\u2500 Check canAccommodateSeatsLocked(selectedRequest.MaxSeats)\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502  \u251c\u2500 If seats exceed ConcurrencyLimit AND executingRequests > 0:\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502  \u2502  CANNOT dispatch yet (must wait for current requests to finish)\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502  \u2514\u2500 Return (nil, nil) \u2192 caller stops dispatching\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2514\u2500 If can accommodate: dequeue from requestsWaiting\n\u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u251c\u2500 Adjust final seats if they exceed concurrency limit\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502  (preserve total work by adjusting additional latency)\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2514\u2500 Update round-robin index to start from selected queue next time\n\u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2514\u2500 Return (selectedQueue, selectedRequest)\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500 Remove request from waiting list:\n\u2502  \u2502  \u251c\u2500 totRequestsWaiting--, totSeatsWaiting -= request.MaxSeats()\n\u2502  \u2502  \u251c\u2500 Metrics: AddRequestsInQueues(-1), AddSeatsInQueues(-maxSeats)\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2514\u2500 request.NoteQueued(false)\n\u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2514\u2500 defer boundNextDispatchLocked(queue) [anti-windup; see 3.5]\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500 Set dispatch decision:\n\u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2514\u2500 If request.decision.Set(decisionExecute) succeeds:\n\u2502     \u2502  (decision promise was unfulfilled; now fulfilled)\n\u2502     \u2502\n\u2502     \u251c\u2500 Move from waiting to executing:\n\u2502     \u2502  \u251c\u2500 request.startTime \u2190 clock.Now()\n\u2502     \u2502  \u251c\u2500 queue.requestsExecuting.Insert(request)\n\u2502     \u2502  \u251c\u2500 queue.seatsInUse += request.MaxSeats()\n\u2502     \u2502  \u251c\u2500 totRequestsExecuting++, totSeatsInUse += request.MaxSeats()\n\u2502     \u2502  \u2514\u2500 Metrics: AddRequestsExecuting(+1), AddSeatConcurrencyInUse(+seats)\n\u2502     \u2502\n\u2502     \u251c\u2500 Advance virtual finish time:\n\u2502     \u2502  \u2502\n\u2502     \u2502  \u2514\u2500 queue.nextDispatchR += request.totalWork()\n\u2502     \u2502     \u2502  \"Cost\" of this request in virtual time\n\u2502     \u2502     \u2502  Larger work \u2192 larger virtual advance \u2192 less priority to future requests\n\u2502     \u2502     \u2502\n\u2502     \u2502     \u2514\u2500 Other queues see this queue recede in virtual time\n\u2502     \u2502\n\u2502     \u2514\u2500 Return true (dispatch succeeded)\n\u2502\n\u2514\u2500 Return false (if decision.Set failed or no queue candidate)\n   \u2502  Caller will retry this request once another finishes\n   \u2502\n   \u2514\u2500 (Can only happen if request's context was canceled before dispatch)\n```\n\n### 3.3 Virtual Time Progression: `syncTimeLocked()` (queueset.go:465\u2013522)\n\nVirtual time advances proportionally to concurrency limits and active queue load:\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500 syncTimeLocked(ctx)\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500 Measure elapsed real time:\n\u2502  \u2502  realNow := clock.Now()\n\u2502  \u2502  timeSinceLast := realNow - lastRealTime\n\u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2514\u2500 lastRealTime \u2190 realNow\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500 Compute virtual time advancement rate:\n\u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2514\u2500 getVirtualTimeRatioLocked()\n\u2502     \u2502\n\u2502     \u251c\u2500 activeQueues \u2190 count of non-empty queues\n\u2502     \u2502\n\u2502     \u251c\u2500 seatsRequested \u2190 \u2211(queue.seatsInUse + queue.requestsWaiting.MaxSeatsSum)\n\u2502     \u2502\n\u2502     \u251c\u2500 If activeQueues == 0:\n\u2502     \u2502  \u2502  return 0 (no advancement while idle)\n\u2502     \u2502  \u2502\n\u2502     \u2502  \u2514\u2500 No virtual time consumption\n\u2502     \u2502\n\u2502     \u2514\u2500 Else:\n\u2502        return min(seatsRequested, ConcurrencyLimit) / activeQueues\n\u2502        \u2502\n\u2502        \u2502  Each active queue \"consumes\" an equal share of concurrency\n\u2502        \u2502  Unmet demand (seatsRequested > limit) means queues share fairly\n\u2502        \u2502  Unmet demand (seatsRequested < limit) means virtual time = real time\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500 Advance global progress meter:\n\u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2514\u2500 currentR += SeatsTimesDuration(ratio, timeSinceLast)\n\u2502     \u2502  Converts: (seats/queue) \u00d7 (elapsed time) \u2192 seat-seconds\n\u2502     \u2502  Uses fixed-point SeatSeconds (scale = 1e8)\n\u2502\n\u2514\u2500 If currentR >= highR (overflow threshold):\n   \u2502\n   \u2514\u2500 advanceEpoch(ctx, realNow, incrR)\n      \u2502  Decrement currentR and all queue.nextDispatchR by rDecrement (2^63)\n      \u2502  Prevents uint64 overflow\n      \u2502  Idempotent for queues that become empty\n      \u2502\n      \u2514\u2500 [See Section 3.5 for anti-windup implications]\n```\n\n**Key insight:** Virtual time rate is `(fair share of concurrency) / (queue count)`. If 4 queues compete for 100-seat limit, each queue \"time\" advances at 25 seats/sec in real time, regardless of actual demand. This provides proportional fairness.\n\n### 3.4 Request Completion: `finishRequestLocked()` (queueset.go:863\u2013943)\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500 finishRequestLocked(req)\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500 Update counters:\n\u2502  \u2502  \u251c\u2500 totRequestsExecuting--\n\u2502  \u2502  \u251c\u2500 Metrics: AddRequestsExecuting(-1)\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2514\u2500 actualServiceDuration := now - req.startTime\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500 Determine seat release timing:\n\u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2514\u2500 If AdditionalLatency <= 0:\n\u2502     \u2502  Release all seats immediately\n\u2502     \u2502\n\u2502     \u2514\u2500 releaseSeatsLocked():\n\u2502        \u251c\u2500 totSeatsInUse -= req.MaxSeats()\n\u2502        \u251c\u2500 req.queue.seatsInUse -= req.MaxSeats()\n\u2502        \u251c\u2500 Metrics: AddSeatConcurrencyInUse(-seats)\n\u2502        \u2514\u2500 Call removeQueueIfEmptyLocked() [queue housekeeping]\n\u2502\n\u2502  Else:\n\u2502     \u2502\n\u2502     \u251c\u2500 Release InitialSeats immediately\n\u2502     \u2502\n\u2502     \u251c\u2500 Schedule deferred release of FinalSeats after AdditionalLatency\n\u2502     \u2502  \u2502  via clock.EventAfterDuration(func() { releaseSeatsLocked() }, AdditionalLatency)\n\u2502     \u2502  \u2502\n\u2502     \u2502  \u2514\u2500 Client perceives no latency; seats held invisibly in background\n\u2502     \u2502\n\u2502     \u2514\u2500 Post-release: dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500 Adjust queue's virtual start time (anti-windup):\n\u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2514\u2500 If req was dispatched from a queue:\n\u2502     \u2502\n\u2502     \u2514\u2500 queue.nextDispatchR -= SeatsTimesDuration(req.InitialSeats,\n\u2502        EstimatedServiceDuration - actualServiceDuration)\n\u2502        \u2502\n\u2502        \u2502  Rationale:\n\u2502        \u2502  - Estimated cost: initialSeats \u00d7 estimatedServiceDuration\n\u2502        \u2502  - Actual cost: initialSeats \u00d7 actualServiceDuration\n\u2502        \u2502  - Difference: credit back to queue if actual < estimated\n\u2502        \u2502\n\u2502        \u2514\u2500 Reduces queue's virtual start time \u2192 increases dispatch priority\n\u2502\n\u2514\u2500 Remove request from queue:\n   \u2502\n   \u251c\u2500 If queued: queue.requestsExecuting.Delete(req)\n   \u2502\n   \u2514\u2500 If not queued (concurrency-only mode):\n      \u2514\u2500 requestsExecutingSet.Delete(req)\n```\n\n### 3.5 Anti-Windup: `boundNextDispatchLocked()` (queueset.go:952\u2013964)\n\n**Problem:** A queue that cannot use all its allocated concurrency (e.g., bursty single-stream) accumulates a decreasing virtual start time (its `nextDispatchR`), gaining unfair priority over busier queues. The anti-windup bounds this:\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500 boundNextDispatchLocked(queue)\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500 If queue is now empty: return (no action needed)\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500 Peek oldest waiting request:\n\u2502  \u2502  oldestReqFromMinQueue := queue.requestsWaiting.Peek()\n\u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2514\u2500 virtualStartBound := oldestReqFromMinQueue.arrivalR\n\u2502     \u2502  (request cannot start before it arrives)\n\u2502\n\u2514\u2500 If queue.nextDispatchR < virtualStartBound:\n   \u2502\n   \u251c\u2500 queue.nextDispatchR \u2190 virtualStartBound\n   \u2502\n   \u2514\u2500 Log: \"AntiWindup tweaked queue\" with delta\n      \u2502\n      \u2514\u2500 Prevents dispatch before arrival\n```\n\n**Rationale:** If a queue is idle (no requests), its virtual time would advance unbounded. When a new request arrives, we clamp the queue's virtual start \u2265 arrival time. This prevents \"catching up\" too much.\n\n### 3.6 Request Waiting and Decision: `request.wait()` (queueset.go:397\u2013441)\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500 req.wait() [called by req.Finish() to get dispatch decision]\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500 Fetch decision promise:\n\u2502  \u2502  decisionAny := req.decision.Get()\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502  Blocks until decision is fulfilled (by dispatchLocked or timeout)\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2514\u2500 Lock queueset and sync virtual time\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500 If decision == decisionExecute:\n\u2502  \u2502  return (true, false)  \u2190 execute the request\n\u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2514\u2500 Caller's execFn() will run immediately\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500 Else (decision == decisionCancel, due to context timeout/cancel):\n\u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u251c\u2500 Remove request from queue:\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502  queue.requestsWaiting.Length()--\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502  totSeatsWaiting -= req.MaxSeats()\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2514\u2500 Metrics: AddReject(..., \"time-out\")\n\u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2514\u2500 return (false, isIdleLocked())  \u2190 request was rejected (timed out)\n\u2502\n\u2514\u2500 Note: Cannot call wait() twice on same request (enforced)\n```\n\n---\n\n## 4. Fairness Algorithm Details\n\n### 4.1 Fair Queuing Foundations\n\nThe QueueSet implements a variant of **Weighted Fair Queuing (WFQ)**. The key idea:\n\n1. **Virtual Time (R):** A monotonically increasing counter measuring work allocated\n2. **Virtual Start/Finish:** Each request has a virtual arrival time (`arrivalR`) and virtual finish time (`arrivalR + totalWork`)\n3. **Selection Rule:** Always dispatch the request with minimum virtual finish time\n4. **Guarantee:** Over long timescales, each flow receives service proportional to its demand (up to fair share)\n\n**Example:**\n- Request A: work = 10 seat-seconds, arrives at R=0 \u2192 finishes at R=10\n- Request B: work = 20 seat-seconds, arrives at R=0 \u2192 finishes at R=20\n- Dispatch order: A (finish@10), then B (finish@20)\n- If another A arrives at R=10: A2 finishes at R=20 (same as B)\n- Fair: both flows receive equal service time\n\n### 4.2 Virtual Time Rate Adaptation\n\nInstead of fixed-weight fair queuing, the QueueSet uses **dynamic virtual time progression** based on concurrency limits and load:\n\n```\nvirtual_time_rate = min(seatsRequested, concurrencyLimit) / activeQueues\n```\n\n**Implications:**\n\n| Scenario | seatsRequested | activeQueues | Rate per Queue |\n|----------|----------------|--------------|----------------|\n| 4 queues, 100 seats | 100 | 4 | 25 seats/sec |\n| 4 queues, 40 seats | 40 | 4 | 10 seats/sec |\n| 4 queues, 200 seats | 200 | 4 | 25 seats/sec (clamped) |\n| 2 queues, 100 seats | 100 | 2 | 50 seats/sec |\n\n**Effect:** Queues with low demand don't slow down others. Queues sharing the limit get equal virtual time.\n\n### 4.3 Work Estimation and Seat-Seconds\n\nWork is measured in **seat-seconds**, a two-phase model:\n\n```\ntotalWork = InitialSeats \u00d7 EstimatedServiceDuration\n          + FinalSeats \u00d7 AdditionalLatency\n\nExample:\n  ListRequest with 1000 objects\n  InitialSeats=3, EstimatedServiceDuration=3ms \u2192 9ms-seats\n  FinalSeats=1, AdditionalLatency=0 \u2192 0ms-seats\n  Total work = 9 ms-seats\n```\n\n**Why two phases?**\n- **Initial phase:** Request actively uses concurrency (network send, compute)\n- **Final phase:** Minimal active use; seats held for flow completion guarantees (e.g., TCP RST handling)\n\n### 4.4 Shuffle Sharding: Load Balancing Among Queues\n\nShuffle sharding solves a crucial problem: **head-of-line blocking**. Without it, a single slow request from flow X blocks all other requests from X.\n\n**Algorithm** (shuffleShardLocked, queueset.go:583\u2013612):\n\n```\n1. dealer.DealIntoHand(hashValue, handSize)\n   \u2502  Input: flow's hash, desired hand size (e.g., 8)\n   \u2502  Output: array of queue indices (e.g., [3, 7, 1, 5, 2, 8, 0, 4])\n   \u2502\n   \u2502  Ensures: different flows get different hands, but hands overlap\n   \u2502           (reduces collision probability vs. simple hash mod)\n\n2. Iterate through hand, selecting queue with minimum TotalWorkSum\n   \u2502  offset := enqueues % handSize  (round-robin offset for fairness)\n   \u2502  For i = 0 to handSize-1:\n   \u2502    queueIdx := hand[(offset + i) % handSize]\n   \u2502    if queueSum[queueIdx].TotalWorkSum < minQueueWorkSum:\n   \u2502      bestQueueIdx \u2190 queueIdx\n\n3. Enqueue into bestQueueIdx\n\nOutcome:\n  - Same flow always gets queued to one of its hand's queues\n  - Requests from different flows spread across queues\n  - Load balancing: pick least-loaded queue from hand\n  - Starvation prevention: offset ensures round-robin fairness among hand members\n```\n\n**Trade-off:** Shuffle sharding trades determinism for fairness. A flow may experience variable queueing if its hand happens to be congested.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Failure Modes, Limits, and Design Tradeoffs\n\n### 5.1 Overflow Management\n\n**Problem:** Virtual time `R` is a `uint64`. After ~584 CPU-years of continuous operation, it overflows.\n\n**Solution:** Epoch advancement (advanceEpoch, queueset.go:492\u2013522)\n\n```\nTrigger: currentR >= highR (where highR = 2^63 + 2^62)\n\nAction:\n  1. Subtract rDecrement (2^63) from:\n     - currentR\n     - All queue.nextDispatchR\n     - All request.arrivalR (for queued requests)\n\n  2. Log the event with old/new values and integrity check\n\nRationale:\n  - Preserves relative ordering (A - C == (A-D) - (C-D))\n  - Resets counter, extending lifetime to another ~584 years\n  - Idempotent for empty queues (nextDispatchR \u2192 0 if queue unused)\n```\n\n**Risk:** If any adjustment underflows (detected and logged), fairness metrics become unreliable, but scheduling continues.\n\n### 5.2 Seat Accommodation and Borrowing Limits\n\n**Problem:** A request may require more seats than the concurrency limit.\n\n**Handling** (canAccommodateSeatsLocked, queueset.go:748\u2013769):\n\n```\nCase 1: DesiredNumQueues < 0 (exempt from limitation)\n  \u2192 Always return true (admit request immediately)\n\nCase 2: RequestSeats > ConcurrencyLimit\n  \u2192 If totRequestsExecuting == 0: admit (allow one to start)\n  \u2192 Else: reject (wait for current requests to finish)\n\nCase 3: RequestSeats + TotSeatsInUse <= ConcurrencyLimit\n  \u2192 Admit (sufficient capacity)\n\nCase 4: RequestSeats + TotSeatsInUse > ConcurrencyLimit\n  \u2192 Reject (insufficient capacity, must wait)\n```\n\n**Trade-off:** Case 2 allows a single request to exceed the limit, but prevents cascading overflow. This violates strict concurrency control but ensures liveness.\n\n### 5.3 Virtual Dispatch Start (Anti-Windup) Limitations\n\n**Problem:** A queue that alternates between idle and active can accumulate a very early `nextDispatchR`, gaining unfair priority.\n\n**Partial mitigation:** boundNextDispatchLocked bounds `nextDispatchR \u2265 oldestWaitingRequest.arrivalR`.\n\n**Limitation:** This bound is conservative. If a queue is idle for 1 hour, then receives a request, its virtual start is bumped to the current virtual time, but by then global virtual time has advanced ~10^6 seat-seconds. The queue may have gained priority unfairly.\n\n**Why not fully resync?** Setting `nextDispatchR = currentR` for each idle queue would be too aggressive, allowing \"fresh\" queues to cut in line.\n\n### 5.4 Queue Attrition and Configuration Changes\n\n**Problem:** If desired number of queues decreases, we can't immediately remove occupied queues.\n\n**Handling** (setConfiguration, queueset.go:254\u2013287):\n\n```\nIf DesiredNumQueues decreases from 10 to 5:\n  1. Do not remove extra queues immediately\n  2. Only remove queues when they become empty (attrition)\n  3. Other queue parameters (QueueLengthLimit) frozen while removing queues\n```\n\n**Trade-off:** Transient over-provisioning until queues drain. Memory impact is bounded by queue count (each queue is ~200 bytes) and request count.\n\n### 5.5 Queue Length Limits and Rejection\n\n**Rejection criteria** (rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked, queueset.go:618\u2013629):\n\n```\nReject if:\n  totSeatsInUse >= ConcurrencyLimit AND\n  curQueueLength >= QueueLengthLimit\n\nRationale:\n  - Prevent unbounded queue growth (memory DOS)\n  - Allow queueing when concurrency is available (latency isolation)\n  - Admit if either constraint has room\n```\n\n**Problem:** This is an AND condition, not OR. If concurrency limit is hit but queue is short, request is admitted. If queue is full but concurrency available, request is admitted. Only when both are maxed is it rejected.\n\n**Justification:** Reduces unfair rejection during transient overload.\n\n### 5.6 Estimation Error and Service Time Feedback\n\n**Problem:** `EstimatedServiceDuration` is fixed (default 3ms) per queueset. Actual service times vary widely.\n\n**Feedback mechanism** (finishRequestLocked, queueset.go:937\u2013938):\n\n```\nqueue.nextDispatchR -= SeatsTimesDuration(req.InitialSeats,\n                                           estimatedServiceDuration - actualServiceDuration)\n```\n\n**Effect:** If actual < estimated, queue's virtual start decreases (gains priority). If actual > estimated, increases (loses priority).\n\n**Limitation:** Feedback is local to queue; a flow's error doesn't propagate to other queues in the hand. Flow-wide fairness can degrade if one queue overestimates.\n\n### 5.7 Metrics Observation Lag\n\n**Race:** Metrics are updated under lock, but observed external to lock. Between observation and action, state may change.\n\n**Accepted:** This is inherent to sampling metrics. APF clients should not act on single observations.\n\n---\n\n## 6. Extension Points and Customization Hooks\n\n### 6.1 Promise Factory (queueset.go:47\u201354)\n\nThe dispatch decision is encapsulated in a `promise.WriteOnce` (write-once channel with context cancellation).\n\n```go\ntype promiseFactory func(initial interface{}, doneCtx context.Context, doneVal interface{}) promise.WriteOnce\n\nordinaryPromiseFactoryFactory returns promise.NewWriteOnce\n```\n\n**Extension point:** Replace with custom promise implementation for:\n- Custom cancellation behavior (e.g., explicit ack before canceling)\n- Observability (log all decisions)\n- Testing (deterministic decision injection)\n\n**Risk:** Incorrect promise semantics can cause:\n- Deadlock if Set blocks\n- Data races if not thread-safe\n- Request leaks if decision never set\n\n### 6.2 Clock and Virtual Time Control (eventclock.Interface)\n\nQueueSet accepts an `eventclock.Interface` for time operations:\n\n```go\ntype Interface interface {\n  Now() time.Time\n  EventAfterDuration(func(time.Time), time.Duration)\n  ...\n}\n```\n\n**Extension point:** Inject custom clock for:\n- **Testing:** Mock time, fast-forward virtual time\n- **Simulation:** Custom virtual time rates\n- **Observability:** Instrument all time-related decisions\n\n**Risk:**\n- Incorrect `EventAfterDuration` timing \u2192 seat leaks (never released)\n- Time going backward \u2192 underflow detection, integrity warnings\n\n### 6.3 Work Estimator (request/width.go)\n\nRequest work is estimated by pluggable `WorkEstimatorFunc`:\n\n```go\ntype WorkEstimatorFunc func(*http.Request, flowSchemaName, priorityLevelName string) WorkEstimate\n```\n\n**Extensions (already in codebase):**\n- `listWorkEstimator`: Estimates based on object count (calls statsGetter)\n- `mutatingWorkEstimator`: Estimates based on watcher count (calls watchCountGetter)\n- Fallback: Default 1 seat for unknown request types\n\n**Customization hooks:**\n```go\nmaxSeatsFunc := func(priorityLevelName string) uint64 { ... }\nstatsGetter := func(resourceName string) (storage.Stats, error) { ... }\nwatchCountGetter := func(requestInfo *RequestInfo) int { ... }\n```\n\n**Risk:**\n- Overestimating work \u2192 false seat exhaustion, unnecessary queueing\n- Underestimating work \u2192 true overload with poor fairness\n- Non-deterministic estimates \u2192 unpredictable fairness\n\n### 6.4 Shuffle Sharding Dealer (shufflesharding/shufflesharding.go)\n\nShuffle sharding hand selection is delegated to `shufflesharding.Dealer`:\n\n```go\ntype Dealer interface {\n  DealIntoHand(hashValue uint64, backHand []int) []int\n}\n```\n\n**Extension point:** Custom hand-dealing algorithms for:\n- Weighted sharding (some queues get larger hands)\n- Topology-aware sharding (prefer low-latency queues)\n- Adaptive hand sizing (adjust based on collision rates)\n\n**Risk:** Collisions in hand assignment can cause starvation if multiple flows map to same queue.\n\n### 6.5 Metrics Observability (metrics.go)\n\nAll state changes are reported to metrics:\n\n```go\nmetrics.AddRequestsInQueues(ctx, qsName, fsName, delta)\nmetrics.AddSeatsInQueues(ctx, qsName, fsName, delta)\nmetrics.SetDispatchMetrics(qsName, currentR, nextDispatchR, ...)\nmetrics.AddEpochAdvance(ctx, qsName, success)\n```\n\n**Extension point:** Hook metrics subsystem to:\n- Export to custom monitoring backend (Prometheus, CloudMonitoring)\n- Trigger alerts on fairness violations\n- Log detailed dispatch decisions\n\n**Risk:** Metrics callback errors will not cause rejection, but may slow down hot paths.\n\n---\n\n## 7. Operational Implications: Performance, Reliability, and Maintainability\n\n### 7.1 Concurrency and Locking Strategy\n\n**Lock design:**\n- Single `sync.Mutex` per queueset protects all mutable state\n- Lock held during:\n  - Initial request ingress (StartRequest)\n  - Virtual time updates (syncTimeLocked)\n  - All dispatch operations\n  - Request finish handling\n\n**Lock release:**\n- Lock released immediately after decision is made\n- Actual request execution runs outside lock\n- Decision delivery (promise.Get) doesn't hold lock\n\n**Performance implications:**\n```\nLock contention = (arrival rate) \u00d7 (average time in critical section)\n\nTypical: ~1\u03bcs per StartRequest + ~100ns per syncTimeLocked\n         With 10k req/s: ~10ms contention per second (acceptable)\n\nWorst case: Large queuesets (100+ queues) with high arrival rates\n            Round-robin dispatch loop scales O(queues) per dispatch\n            With 1000 queues: ~5\u03bcs per dispatch\n```\n\n**Mitigation:** Lock-free data structures for queue peeking (future work).\n\n### 7.2 Memory Footprint\n\nPer queueset:\n- `queueSet` struct: ~500 bytes\n- Per queue: ~200 bytes (FIFO list, sync.Set)\n- Per request: ~256 bytes (context, metadata, promise)\n\n**Example:** 100 queues + 1000 waiting requests = 100\u00d7200 + 1000\u00d7256 = ~280KB\n\n**Scalability:** Memory grows with O(queues + waiting requests). No inherent limits; configured via QueueLengthLimit.\n\n### 7.3 Virtual Time Stability\n\n**Risk:** Overflow, underflow, or monotonicity violations can corrupt fairness.\n\n**Safeguards:**\n1. **Epoch advancement:** Detects overflow, logs warnings if underflow occurs during decrement\n2. **Monotonicity checks:** `boundNextDispatchLocked` asserts `nextDispatchR >= arrivalR`\n3. **Metrics correlation:** Dispatch metrics include virtual time (external monitoring can alert)\n\n**Operational alert:** If `epoch_advance_errors` > 0, investigate virtual time corruption.\n\n### 7.4 Tuning Parameters and Trade-offs\n\n| Parameter | Location | Impact | Notes |\n|-----------|----------|--------|-------|\n| `DesiredNumQueues` | QueuingConfig | Fairness, latency | Higher \u2192 better fairness, higher overhead |\n| `HandSize` | QueuingConfig | Collision, predictability | Higher \u2192 lower collision, higher shuffle cost |\n| `QueueLengthLimit` | QueuingConfig | Memory, rejection rate | Higher \u2192 more memory, less rejection |\n| `ConcurrencyLimit` | DispatchingConfig | Throughput, latency | Sweet spot depends on hardware |\n| `EstimatedServiceDuration` | queueset.go:215 | Seat allocation fairness | Too high \u2192 underutilization; too low \u2192 overload |\n\n### 7.5 Observability Checklist\n\n**Key metrics to monitor:**\n1. **`apiserver_priority_level_request_utilization`**: Executing requests / limit (target: 0.7\u20130.9)\n2. **`apiserver_priority_level_seat_utilization`**: Occupied seats / limit (target: 0.6\u20130.8)\n3. **`apiserver_priority_level_request_wait_duration`**: P50, P99 queueing latency\n4. **`apiserver_request_total` with `code=429`**: Rejected requests (trending up = concern)\n5. **`apiserver_priority_level_queued_requests`**: Requests waiting (should be < QueueLengthLimit \u00d7 DesiredNumQueues / 2)\n6. **`apiserver_priority_level_epoch_advance_total`**: Epoch advancements (OK to see every 1\u201310 seconds under load)\n7. **`apiserver_flowschema_dispatched_requests_total`**: By flow schema (check for fairness across flows)\n\n### 7.6 Debugging and Introspection\n\n**Available methods:**\n- `queueSet.Dump(includeRequestDetails bool)`: Snapshots internal state (lock held during snapshot)\n  - Returns requests in queues, executing requests, virtual times, seat counts\n  - Safe for live queries (not async)\n\n**Limitations:**\n- Dump is point-in-time; state changes immediately after\n- No time-series; must sample repeatedly\n- Expensive for large request counts (O(requests) to snapshot)\n\n**Debug endpoints:**\n- `/debug/api_priority_and_fairness/`: Exposes queueset dump via HTTP (if installed)\n\n**Manual troubleshooting:**\n```bash\n# Check if QueueSet is overloaded\ncurl http://localhost:6443/debug/api_priority_and_fairness/dump_queues\n# High: totRequestsWaiting, high: seatsInUse / ConcurrencyLimit\n\n# Check if shuffle sharding is unbalanced\njq '.queues[] | {queue: .index, waiting: (.requests | length), executing}' < dump.json\n# Unbalanced queue lengths indicate collision issues\n\n# Check virtual time advancement\ncurl ... | jq '.queues[] | .nextDispatchR'\n# Should be in ascending order (monotonic); gaps indicate idle queues\n```\n\n### 7.7 Failure Scenarios and Recovery\n\n| Scenario | Symptom | Cause | Recovery |\n|----------|---------|-------|----------|\n| Request stuck waiting | P99 latency spike, single request doesn't finish | Context timeout or handler crash | Request context timeout will trigger cancellation |\n| Queue length limit hit | Requests rejected with 429 | Load > ConcurrencyLimit \u00d7 DesiredNumQueues / QueueLengthLimit | Reduce load or increase limits |\n| Virtual time overflow | `epoch_advance` warnings in logs | Continuous overload for weeks | Restart API server (resets R) or increase epoch threshold |\n| Memory leak | RAM usage grows unbounded | Requests not calling Finish() | Operator must restart affected server |\n| Unfair dispatch | One flow dominates execution | Hand collision or work estimation error | Check metrics, adjust HandSize or estimator |\n\n---\n\n## 8. Architecture Map: Critical Files and Their Responsibilities\n\n```\nstaging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 fairqueuing/\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 interface.go                    # QueueSet, Request, Config interfaces\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 queueset/\n\u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 queueset.go                 # Main logic: StartRequest, dispatch, virtual time\n\u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 types.go                    # request, queue, queueSum structs\n\u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 fifo_list.go                # requestFIFO: O(1) queue with running sums\n\u2502   \u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 queueset_test.go            # fairness and fairness validation\n\u2502   \u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 fifo_list_test.go\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 eventclock/                     # eventclock.Interface for time operations\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 promise/                        # promise.WriteOnce for deferred decisions\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 request/\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 width.go                        # WorkEstimate, WorkEstimatorFunc\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 seat_seconds.go                 # SeatSeconds: fixed-point work metric\n\u2502   \u251c\u2500\u2500 list_work_estimator.go          # Per-list-size work estimation\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 mutating_work_estimator.go      # Per-watcher work estimation\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 apf_controller.go                   # Main controller: config syncing, priority level state\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 apf_filter.go                       # Request entry point: Handle(), dispatcher\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 apf_controller_debug.go             # Debug endpoints\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 metrics/\n\u2502   \u2514\u2500\u2500 metrics.go                      # Metrics recording: requests, seats, latencies\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 debug/\n    \u2514\u2500\u2500 ...                             # Dump structures and HTTP debug handler\n\nk8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/shufflesharding/\n\u251c\u2500\u2500 shufflesharding.go                  # Dealer: shuffle-sharded hand allocation\n\u2514\u2500\u2500 shufflesharding_test.go\n```\n\n**Key entry points:**\n1. **`apf_filter.go: Handle()`** \u2192 Called by HTTP handler for each request\n2. **`apf_controller.go: startRequest()`** \u2192 Routes to QueueSet.StartRequest()\n3. **`queueset.go: StartRequest()`** \u2192 Main ingress; enqueues and dispatches\n4. **`queueset.go: dispatchLocked()`** \u2192 Fair queue selection and virtual time advancement\n5. **`request.Finish()`** \u2192 Client callback; calls queueSet.finishRequestAndDispatchAsMuchAsPossible()\n\n---\n\n## 9. Conclusion\n\nThe APF QueueSet is a sophisticated fair-queuing implementation adapted for multi-phase request execution and work-aware concurrency control. Its fairness guarantees rest on:\n\n1. **Virtual time scheduling** (fair queuing algorithm)\n2. **Dynamic rate adaptation** (proportional to concurrency limit and queue count)\n3. **Shuffle sharding** (load balancing and collision resistance)\n4. **Work estimation** (seat-seconds accounting)\n5. **Anti-windup mechanisms** (preventing unfair idle-queue priority)\n\n**Strengths:**\n- Provably fair under steady-state assumptions\n- Handles variable request widths (multi-phase execution)\n- Adaptive to load (virtual time rate adjusts)\n- Configurable fairness/performance tradeoff (queue count, hand size)\n\n**Limitations:**\n- Single global lock (contention under extreme load)\n- Fixed work estimator (errors compound across calls)\n- Virtual time is local per queueset (no global fairness across priority levels)\n- Anti-windup is conservative (may allow unfair idle-queue recovery)\n\n**Operational key:** Monitor seat utilization, queue lengths, and dispatch latencies. Tune `DesiredNumQueues` and `ConcurrencyLimit` based on workload characteristics and fairness objectives.\n\n---\n\n## References\n\n- **KEP-1040:** https://github.com/kubernetes/enhancements/blob/master/keps/sig-api-machinery/1040-priority-and-fairness/README.md\n- **Fair Queuing Algorithm (original):** Demers, Keshav, Shenker, \"Analysis and Simulation of a Fair Queueing Algorithm\" (1989)\n- **Shuffle Sharding:** https://dl.acm.org/doi/10.1145/1400519.1400529 (Cushman et al., SIGCOMM 2008)\n",

{
  "content": "# Kubernetes APF QueueSet: Algorithmic Deep-Dive\n\n## Executive Summary\n\nThe QueueSet subsystem implements **Fair Queuing for Server Requests (FQSR)**, a specialized fair-queuing algorithm that multiplexes concurrent API server requests across priority levels. It provides weighted fairness guarantees through virtual time scheduling, shuffle-sharded queue assignment, and adaptive dispatch based on estimated work (seat-seconds). This document traces the end-to-end control flow, dissects the fairness algorithm, and discusses operational tradeoffs.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Subsystem Purpose, Boundaries, and Dependencies\n\n### 1.1 Purpose\n\nThe QueueSet is the **execution scheduling engine** of API Priority and Fairness (APF). It sits between the APF filter (which classifies requests) and the main request handler (which executes them). Its role:\n\n- **Admission control**: Reject or queue requests when concurrency limits are exceeded\n- **Fair dispatch**: Select which queued request executes next, ensuring:\n  - Proportional fairness among flows (via virtual time)\n  - Starvation prevention (via round-robin queue selection)\n  - Work-aware scheduling (via seat-seconds, not just request count)\n- **Concurrency accounting**: Track occupied \"seats\" (a logical concurrency unit) across phases of request execution\n\n### 1.2 Boundaries\n\n**Upstream dependencies:**\n- **APF Controller** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/apf_controller.go`): Provides `QueuingConfig` (desired number of queues, queue length limit, hand size for shuffle sharding) and `DispatchingConfig` (concurrency limit)\n- **Request classifiers**: Extract flow distinguisher and match requests to priority levels\n- **Work estimators** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/request/width.go`): Estimate request width (initial seats, final seats, additional latency) based on request type and payload size\n\n**Downstream dependencies:**\n- **HTTP handler**: Calls `StartRequest()`, then `req.Finish()` when done\n- **Metrics subsystem** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/metrics/`): Observes request counts, seat occupancy, dispatch latencies, rejections\n- **Event clock** (`staging/src/k8s.io/apiserver/pkg/util/flowcontrol/fairqueuing/eventclock/`): Provides virtual time ticking and delayed event scheduling\n\n### 1.3 Key Data Dependencies\n\n- **WorkEstimate**: Carries `InitialSeats` (concurrency during main phase), `FinalSeats` (reserved after execution), and `AdditionalLatency` (padding duration)\n- **SeatSeconds**: Fixed-point representation of work = seats \u00d7 duration, with 1e8 internal scale factor\n- **QueuingConfig**: Encodes desired number of queues (0 = bypass queueing, negative = exempt), queue length limit, shuffle-sharding hand size\n\n---\n\n## 2. Key Components and Responsibility Split\n\n### 2.1 Core Types\n\n#### `queueSet` (queueset.go:85\u2013167)\nThe main orchestrator. Fields include:\n- **`queues []*queue`**: Array of FIFO queues, allocated per shuffle-sharded flow\n- **`currentR fqrequest.SeatSeconds`**: Global virtual time progress meter (R from fair queuing)\n- **`lock sync.Mutex`**: Protects all mutable state\n- **`totSeatsInUse`, `totSeatsWaiting`**: Aggregate seat occupancy\n- **`totRequestsWaiting`, `totRequestsExecuting`**: Request counts for metrics\n- **`dCfg fq.DispatchingConfig`**: Concurrency limits and seat accounting denominators\n- **`promiseFactory`**: Creates decision promises (deferred-write channels for async dispatch decisions)\n\n**Responsibilities:**\n- Initial request ingress and rejection (via `StartRequest()`)\n- Virtual time progression and epoch management\n- Dispatch loop orchestration\n- Request completion tracking and seat release\n\n#### `queue` (types.go:93\u2013110)\nPer-flow-distinguisher queue. Fields:\n- **`requestsWaiting fifo`**: Ordered list of queued requests\n- **`requestsExecuting sets.Set[*request]`**: Executing requests from this queue (for seat tracking)\n- **`nextDispatchR fqrequest.SeatSeconds`**: Virtual finish time of next dispatch from this queue\n- **`seatsInUse int`**: Occupied seats in this queue\n\n**Responsibilities:**\n- FIFO ordering of requests awaiting dispatch\n- Virtual time tracking per queue (anti-windup mechanism)\n\n#### `request` (types.go:33\u201383)\nRequest wrapper with scheduling metadata. Fields:\n- **`decision promise.WriteOnce`**: Deferred decision (execute/cancel)\n- **`arrivalTime`, `startTime`**: Real timestamps for latency metrics\n- **`arrivalR fqrequest.SeatSeconds`**: Virtual time at arrival\n- **`workEstimate completedWorkEstimate`**: Computed total work (initial + final)\n\n**Responsibilities:**\n- Carries request context and work estimate\n- Defers dispatch decision via promise pattern (allows async decision-setting under lock, decision-reading without lock)\n\n#### `requestFIFO` (fifo_list.go:71\u2013156)\nLinked-list FIFO with aggregate statistics. Methods:\n- **`Enqueue(req)`**: Returns `removeFromFIFOFunc` for O(1) removal\n- **`QueueSum()`**: Returns aggregated `InitialSeatsSum`, `MaxSeatsSum`, `TotalWorkSum`\n- **`Walk(func)`**: Iterates without copying (permits removal during iteration)\n\n**Responsibilities:**\n- O(1) enqueue/dequeue/remove operations\n- Maintains running sums of seated widths for shuffle-sharding decisions\n\n---\n\n## 3. End-to-End Control Flow\n\n### 3.1 Request Arrival: `StartRequest()` (queueset.go:308\u2013356)\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500 StartRequest(ctx, workEstimate, hashValue, ...)\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500 Step 0: Check if queueing is bypassed\n\u2502  \u2502  (DesiredNumQueues < 1 \u2192 concurrency-only mode)\n\u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u251c\u2500 If queues disabled:\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2514\u2500 Call canAccommodateSeatsLocked(workEstimate.MaxSeats)\n\u2502  \u2502     \u251c\u2500 If yes: dispatchSansQueueLocked() \u2192 return request (immediate exec)\n\u2502  \u2502     \u2514\u2500 If no: increment totRequestsRejected, return (nil, isIdleLocked)\n\u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2514\u2500 If queues enabled: proceed to Step 1\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500 Step 1: Shuffle-shard and enqueue\n\u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u251c\u2500 shuffleShardAndRejectOrEnqueueLocked()\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502  \u251c\u2500 Call shuffleShardLocked(hashValue)\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502  \u2502  Uses dealer.DealIntoHand(hashValue) to get candidate queues\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502  \u2502  Selects queue with minimum TotalWorkSum (load-balanced assignment)\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502  \u2514\u2500 Return queue index\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502  \u251c\u2500 Create request object with:\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502  \u251c\u2500 arrivalTime \u2190 clock.Now()\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502  \u251c\u2500 arrivalR \u2190 currentR (current virtual time)\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502  \u251c\u2500 decision \u2190 promiseFactory(nil) [decision not yet set]\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502  \u2514\u2500 workEstimate \u2190 completeWorkEstimate(workEstimate)\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502  \u251c\u2500 Call rejectOrEnqueueToBoundLocked(request)\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502  \u251c\u2500 If totSeatsInUse >= concurrencyLimit AND queueLength >= queueLengthLimit:\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502  \u2502  \u2514\u2500 REJECT (return false)\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502  \u2514\u2500 Else: enqueueToBoundLocked(request)\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502     \u251c\u2500 If queue empty: queue.nextDispatchR \u2190 currentR (initialize virtual start)\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502     \u251c\u2500 queue.requestsWaiting.Enqueue(request)\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502     \u251c\u2500 totRequestsWaiting++, totSeatsWaiting += request.MaxSeats()\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502     \u2514\u2500 Metrics: AddRequestsInQueues, AddSeatsInQueues\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2514\u2500 If rejected: return nil\n\u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2514\u2500 If enqueued: proceed to Step 2\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500 Step 2: Immediate dispatch as much as possible\n\u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2514\u2500 dispatchAsMuchAsPossibleLocked()\n\u2502     \u2502  While totRequestsWaiting > 0 AND totSeatsInUse < concurrencyLimit:\n\u2502     \u2502    \u2514\u2500 dispatchLocked() (see Section 3.2)\n\u2502     \u2502\n\u2502     \u2514\u2500 Executes requests from queues until concurrency limit or no queued requests\n\u2502\n\u2514\u2500 Return (request, false)\n   \u2502  If request is nil: caller should reject\n   \u2502  If request is non-nil: caller must call request.Finish() when done\n```\n\n### 3.2 Dispatch: `dispatchLocked()` and Fair Queue Selection (queueset.go:695\u2013743)\n\nFair Queuing uses **virtual time** to achieve fairness. Key insight: dispatch the request whose virtual *finish time* is earliest, ensuring proportional service allocation.\n\n```\n\u250c\u2500 dispatchLocked()\n\u2502\n\u251c\u2500 findDispatchQueueToBoundLocked()\n\u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u251c\u2500 Iterate round-robin through queues\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502  \u2514\u2500 For each queue with waiting requests:\n\u2502  \u2502     \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502     \u251c\u2500 Peek oldest request\n\u2502  \u2502     \u2502\n\u2502  \u2502     \u251c\u2500 Compute currentVirtualFinish:\n\u2502  \u2502
